following variants:</p>/n<div class="mw-highlight mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">/n<pre>/n<span class="kr">ADD</span> <span class="mi">1 </span><span class="kp">TO</span> <span class="nv">x</span>/n<span class="kr">ADD</span> <span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="nv">a</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="nv">b</span> <span class="kp">TO</span> <span class="nv">x</span> <span class="kp">ROUNDED</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="nv">y</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="nv">z</span> <span class="kp">ROUNDED</span>/n/n<span class="kr">ADD</span> <span class="nv">a</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="nv">b</span> <span class="kp">TO</span> <span class="nv">c</span>/n    <span class="kp">ON</span> <span class="kp">SIZE</span> <span class="kp">ERROR</span>/n<span class="kp">       </span> <span class="kr">DISPLAY </span><span class="s2">"Error"</span>/n<span class="kr">END-ADD</span>/n/n<span class="kr">ADD</span> <span class="nv">a</span> <span class="kp">TO</span> <span class="nv">b</span>/n    <span class="ow">NOT</span> <span class="kp">SIZE</span> <span class="kp">ERROR</span>/n<span class="kp">       </span> <span class="kr">DISPLAY </span><span class="s2">"No error"</span>/n    <span class="kp">ON</span> <span class="kp">SIZE</span> <span class="kp">ERROR</span>/n<span class="kp">       </span> <span class="kr">DISPLAY </span><span class="s2">"Error"</span>/n</pre></div>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Code_format">Code format</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=COBOL&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Code format">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<p>COBOL can be written in two formats: fixed (the default) or free. In fixed-format, code must be aligned to fit in certain areas (a hold-over from using punched cards). Until COBOL 2002, these were:</p>/n<table class="wikitable">/n<tr>/n<th>Name</th>/n<th>Column(s)</th>/n<th>Usage</th>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td>Sequence number area</td>/n<td>1–6</td>/n<td>Originally used for card/line numbers, this area is ignored by the compiler</td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td>Indicator area</td>/n<td>7</td>/n<td>The following characters are allowed here:/n<ul>/n<li><code>*</code> – Comment line</li>/n<li><code>/</code> – Comment line that will be printed on a new page of a source listing</li>/n<li><code>-</code> – Continuation line, where words or literals from the previous line are continued</li>/n<li><code>D</code> – Line enabled in debugging mode, which is otherwise ignored</li>/n</ul>/n</td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td>Area A</td>/n<td>8–11</td>/n<td>This contains: <code>DIVISION</code>, <code>SECTION</code> and procedure headers; 01 and 77 level numbers and file/report descriptors</td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td>Area B</td>/n<td>12–72</td>/n<td>Any other code not allowed in Area A</td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td>Program name area</td>/n<td>73–</td>/n<td>Historically up to column 80 for punched cards, it is used to identify the program or sequence the card belongs to</td>/n</tr>/n</table>/n<p>In COBOL 2002, Areas A and B were merged to form the program-text area, which now ends at an implementor-defined column.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42001.C2.A7_F.2_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42001.C2.A7_F.2-109">[106]</a></sup></p>/n<p>COBOL 2002 also introduced free-format code. Free-format code can be placed in any column of the file, as in newer programming languages. Comments are specified using <code>*&gt;</code>, which can be placed anywhere and can also be used in fixed-format source code. Continuation lines are not present, and the <code>&gt;&gt;PAGE</code> directive replaces the <code>/</code> indicator.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42001.C2.A7_F.2_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42001.C2.A7_F.2-109">[106]</a></sup></p>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Identification_division">Identification division</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=COBOL&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Identification division">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<p>The identification division identifies the following code entity and contains the definition of a class or interface.</p>/n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Object-oriented_programming">Object-oriented programming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=COBOL&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Object-oriented programming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>/n<p><a href="/wiki/Class_(computer_programming)" title="Class (computer programming)">Classes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Interface_(object-oriented_programming)" class="mw-redirect" title="Interface (object-oriented programming)">interfaces</a> have been in COBOL since 2002. Classes have factory objects, containing class <a href="/wiki/Method_(computer_programming)" title="Method (computer programming)">methods</a> and variables, and instance objects, containing instance methods and variables.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7_D.18.2_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7_D.18.2-110">[107]</a></sup> Inheritance and interfaces provide <a href="/wiki/Polymorphism_(computer_science)" title="Polymorphism (computer science)">polymorphism</a>. Support for <a href="/wiki/Generic_programming" title="Generic programming">generic programming</a> is provided through parameterized classes, which can be instantiated to use any class or interface. Objects are stored as references which may be restricted to a certain type. There are two ways of calling a method: the <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">INVOKE</code> statement, which acts similarly to <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">CALL</code>, or through inline method invocation, which is analogous to using functions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7_D.18_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7_D.18-111">[108]</a></sup></p>/n<div class="mw-highlight mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">/n<pre>/n<span class="c">*&gt; These are equivalent.</span>/n<span class="kr">INVOKE</span> <span class="nv">my-class</span> <span class="s2">"foo"</span> <span class="kp">RETURNING</span> <span class="nv">var</span>/n<span class="kr">MOVE</span> <span class="nv">my-class</span><span class="p">::</span><span class="s2">"foo"</span> <span class="kp">TO</span> <span class="nv">var</span> <span class="c">*&gt; Inline method invocation</span>/n</pre></div>/n<p>COBOL does not provide a way to <a href="/wiki/Member_visibility" class="mw-redirect" title="Member visibility">hide</a> methods. Class data can be hidden, however, by declaring it without a <a href="/wiki/Property_(programming)" title="Property (programming)"><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">PROPERTY</code></a> clause, which leaves the user with no way to access it.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014108_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014108-112">[109]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Method_overloading" class="mw-redirect" title="Method overloading">Method overloading</a> was added in COBOL 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014896_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014896-113">[110]</a></sup></p>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment_division">Environment division</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=COBOL&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Environment division">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<p>The environment division contains the configuration section and the input-output section. The configuration section is used to specify variable features such as currency signs, locales and character sets. The input-output section contains file-related information.</p>/n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Files">Files</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=COBOL&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Files">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>/n<p>COBOL supports three file formats, or <i><dfn>organizations</dfn></i>: sequential, indexed and relative. In sequential files, records are contiguous and must be traversed <a href="/wiki/Sequential_access" title="Sequential access">sequentially</a>, similarly to a <a href="/wiki/Linked_list" title="Linked list">linked list</a>. Indexed files have one or more indexes which allow records to be <a href="/wiki/Random_access" title="Random access">randomly accessed</a> and which can be sorted on them. Each record must have a <a href="/wiki/Unique_key" title="Unique key">unique key</a>, but other, <i><dfn>alternate</dfn></i>, record keys need not be unique. Implementations of indexed files vary between vendors, although common implementations, such as <a href="/wiki/C-ISAM" class="mw-redirect" title="C-ISAM">C‑ISAM</a> and <a href="/wiki/VSAM" class="mw-redirect" title="VSAM">VSAM</a>, are based on IBM's <a href="/wiki/ISAM" title="ISAM">ISAM</a>. Relative files, like indexed files, have a unique record key, but they do not have alternate keys. A relative record's key is its ordinal position; for example, the 10th record has a key of 10. This means that creating a record with a key of 5 may require the creation of (empty) preceding records. Relative files also allow for both sequential and random access.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7_D.2.1_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7_D.2.1-114">[111]</a></sup></p>/n<p>A common non-standard extension is the <i><dfn>line sequential</dfn></i> organization, used to process text files. Records in a file are terminated by a <a href="/wiki/Newline" title="Newline">newline</a> and may be of varying length.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[112]</a></sup></p>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Data_division">Data division</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=COBOL&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Data division">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<p>The data division is split into six sections which declare different items: the file section, for file records; the working-storage section, for <a href="/wiki/Static_variable" title="Static variable">static variables</a>; the local-storage section, for <a href="/wiki/Automatic_variable" title="Automatic variable">automatic variables</a>; the linkage section, for parameters and the return value; the report section and the screen section, for <a href="/wiki/Text-based_user_interface" title="Text-based user interface">text-based user interfaces</a>.</p>/n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Aggregated_data">Aggregated data</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=COBOL&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Aggregated data">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>/n<p>Data items in COBOL are declared hierarchically through the use of level-numbers which indicate if a data item is part of another. An item with a higher level-number is subordinate to an item with a lower one. Top-level data items, with a level-number of 1, are called <i><dfn>records</dfn></i>. Items that have subordinate aggregate data are called <i><dfn>group items</dfn></i>; those that do not are called <i><dfn>elementary items</dfn></i>. Level-numbers used to describe standard data items are between 1 and 49.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7_8.5.1.2_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7_8.5.1.2-116">[113]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECutler2014Appendix_A_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECutler2014Appendix_A-117">[114]</a></sup></p>/n<div class="mw-highlight mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">/n<pre>/n<span class="c">      </span> <span class="mi">01  </span><span class="nv">some-record</span><span class="p">.</span>                   <span class="c">*&gt; Aggregate group record item</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="mi">05  </span><span class="nv">num</span>            <span class="kt">PIC 9(10)</span><span class="p">.</span>  <span class="c">*&gt; Elementary item</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="mi">05  </span><span class="nv">the-date</span><span class="p">.</span>                  <span class="c">*&gt; Aggregate (sub)group record item</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>         <span class="mi">10  </span><span class="nv">the-year</span>   <span class="kt">PIC 9(4)</span><span class="p">.</span>   <span class="c">*&gt; Elementary item</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>         <span class="mi">10  </span><span class="nv">the-month</span>  <span class="kt">PIC 99</span><span class="p">.</span>     <span class="c">*&gt; Elementary item</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>         <span class="mi">10  </span><span class="nv">the-day</span>    <span class="kt">PIC 99</span><span class="p">.</span>     <span class="c">*&gt; Elementary item</span>/n</pre></div>/n<p>In the above example, elementary item <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">num</code> and group item <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">the-date</code> are subordinate to the record <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">some-record</code>, while elementary items <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">the-year</code>, <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">the-month</code>, and <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">the-day</code> are part of the group item <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">the-date</code>.</p>/n<p>Subordinate items can be disambiguated with the <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">IN</code> (or <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">OF</code>) keyword. For example, consider the example code above along with the following example:</p>/n<div class="mw-highlight mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">/n<pre>/n<span class="c">      </span> <span class="mi">01  </span><span class="nv">sale-date</span><span class="p">.</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="mi">05  </span><span class="nv">the-year</span>       <span class="kt">PIC 9(4)</span><span class="p">.</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="mi">05  </span><span class="nv">the-month</span>      <span class="kt">PIC 99</span><span class="p">.</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="mi">05  </span><span class="nv">the-day</span>        <span class="kt">PIC 99</span><span class="p">.</span>/n</pre></div>/n<p>The names <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">the-year</code>, <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">the-month</code>, and <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">the-day</code> are ambiguous by themselves, since more than one data item is defined with those names. To specify a particular data item, for instance one of the items contained within the <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">sale-date</code> group, the programmer would use <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">the-year IN sale-date</code> (or the equivalent <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">the-year OF sale-date</code>). (This syntax is similar to the "dot notation" supported by most contemporary languages.)</p>/n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_data_levels">Other data levels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=COBOL&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Other data levels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>/n<p>A level-number of 66 is used to declare a re-grouping of previously defined items, irrespective of how those items are structured. This data level, also referred to by the associated <dfn><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">RENAMES</code> clause</dfn>, is rarely used<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[115]</a></sup> and, circa 1988, was usually found in old programs. Its ability to ignore the hierarchical and logical structure data meant its use was not recommended and many installations forbade its use.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcCrackenGolden1988.C2.A7_19.9_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcCrackenGolden1988.C2.A7_19.9-119">[116]</a></sup></p>/n<div class="mw-highlight mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">/n<pre>/n<span class="c">      </span> <span class="mi">01  </span><span class="nv">customer-record</span><span class="p">.</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="mi">05  </span><span class="nv">cust-key</span>            <span class="kt">PIC X(10)</span><span class="p">.</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="mi">05  </span><span class="nv">cust-name</span><span class="p">.</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>         <span class="mi">10  </span><span class="nv">cust-first-name</span> <span class="kt">PIC X(30)</span><span class="p">.</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>         <span class="mi">10  </span><span class="nv">cust-last-name</span>  <span class="kt">PIC X(30)</span><span class="p">.</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="mi">05  </span><span class="nv">cust-dob</span>            <span class="kt">PIC 9(8)</span><span class="p">.</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="mi">05  </span><span class="nv">cust-balance</span>        <span class="kt">PIC 9(7)V99</span><span class="p">.</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>     /n<span class="c">      </span> <span class="mi">66  </span><span class="nv">cust-personal-details</span>   <span class="kp">RENAMES</span> <span class="nv">cust-name</span> <span class="kp">THRU</span> <span class="nv">cust-dob</span><span class="p">.</span>/n<span class="c">      </span> <span class="mi">66  </span><span class="nv">cust-all-details</span>        <span class="kp">RENAMES</span> <span class="nv">cust-name</span> <span class="kp">THRU</span> <span class="nv">cust-balance</span><span class="p">.</span>/n</pre></div>/n<p>A 77 level-number indicates the item is stand-alone, and in such situations is equivalent to the level-number 01. For example, the following code declares two 77-level data items, <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">property-name</code> and <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">sales-region</code>, which are non-group data items that are independent of (not subordinate to) any other data items:</p>/n<div class="mw-highlight mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">/n<pre>/n<span class="c">      </span> <span class="mi">77  </span><span class="nv">property-name</span>      <span class="kt">PIC X(80)</span><span class="p">.</span>/n<span class="c">      </span> <span class="mi">77  </span><span class="nv">sales-region</span>       <span class="kt">PIC 9(5)</span><span class="p">.</span>/n</pre></div>/n<p>An 88 level-number declares a <i><dfn>condition name</dfn></i> (a so-called 88-level) which is true when its parent data item contains one of the values specified in its <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">VALUE</code> clause.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECutler2014.C2.A7_5.8.5_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECutler2014.C2.A7_5.8.5-120">[117]</a></sup> For example, the following code defines two 88-level condition-name items that are true or false depending on the current character data value of the <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">wage-type</code> data item. When the data item contains a value of <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">'H'</code>, the condition-name <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">wage-is-hourly</code> is true, whereas when it contains a value of <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">'S'</code> or <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">'Y'</code>, the condition-name <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">wage-is-yearly</code> is true. If the data item contains some other value, both of the condition-names are false.</p>/n<div class="mw-highlight mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">/n<pre>/n<span class="c">      </span> <span class="mi">01  </span><span class="nv">wage-type</span>          <span class="kt">PIC X</span><span class="p">.</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="mi">88  </span><span class="nv">wage-is-hourly</span> <span class="kp">VALUE </span><span class="s2">"H"</span><span class="p">.</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="mi">88  </span><span class="nv">wage-is-yearly</span> <span class="kp">VALUE </span><span class="s2">"S"</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="s2">"Y"</span><span class="p">.</span>/n</pre></div>/n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Data_types">Data types</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=COBOL&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Data types">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>/n<p>Standard COBOL provides the following data types:<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7_8.5.2_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7_8.5.2-121">[118]</a></sup></p>/n<table class="wikitable">/n<tr>/n<th>Data type</th>/n<th>Sample declaration</th>/n<th>Notes</th>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td>Alphabetic</td>/n<td><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="kt">PIC A(30)</span></code></td>/n<td>May only contain letters or spaces</td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td>Alphanumeric</td>/n<td><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="kt">PIC X(30)</span></code></td>/n<td>May contain any characters</td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td>Boolean</td>/n<td><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="kt">PIC 1</span> <span class="kp">USAGE</span> <span class="err">BIT</span></code></td>/n<td>Data stored in the form of 0s and 1s, as a binary number</td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td>Index</td>/n<td><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="kp">USAGE</span> <span class="kp">INDEX</span></code></td>/n<td>Used to reference table elements</td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td>National</td>/n<td><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="kt">PIC N(30)</span></code></td>/n<td>Similar to alphanumeric, but using an extended character set, e.g. <a href="/wiki/UTF-8" title="UTF-8">UTF-8</a></td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td>Numeric</td>/n<td><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="kt">PIC 9(5)V9(5)</span></code></td>/n<td>May contain only numbers</td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td>Object</td>/n<td><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="kp">USAGE</span> <span class="err">OBJECT</span> <span class="kp">REFERENCE</span></code></td>/n<td>May reference either an object or <code>NULL</code></td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td>Pointer</td>/n<td><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="kp">USAGE</span> <span class="kp">POINTER</span></code></td>/n<td></td>/n</tr>/n</table>/n<p>Type safety is variable in COBOL. Numeric data is converted between different representations and sizes silently and alphanumeric data can be placed in any data item that can be stored as a string, including numeric and group data.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7_14.9.24_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7_14.9.24-122">[119]</a></sup> In contrast, object references and pointers may only be assigned from items of the same type and their values may be restricted to a certain type.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7_14.9.35_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7_14.9.35-123">[120]</a></sup></p>/n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="PICTURE_clause">PICTURE clause</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=COBOL&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: PICTURE clause">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>/n<p>A <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">PICTURE</code> (or <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">PIC</code>) clause is a string of characters, each of which represents a portion of the data item and what it may contain. Some picture characters specify the type of the item and how many characters or digits it occupies in memory. For example, a <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">9</code> indicates a decimal digit, and an <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">S</code> indicates that the item is <a href="/wiki/Signedness" title="Signedness">signed</a>. Other picture characters (called <i><dfn>insertion</dfn></i> and <i><dfn>editing</dfn></i> characters) specify how an item should be formatted. For example, a series of <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">+</code> characters define character positions as well as how a leading sign character is to be positioned within the final character data; the rightmost non-numeric character will contain the item's sign, while other character positions corresponding to a <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">+</code> to the left of this position will contain a space. Repeated characters can be specified more concisely by specifying a number in parentheses after a picture character; for example, <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">9(7)</code> is equivalent to <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">9999999</code>. Picture specifications containing only digit (<code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">9</code>) and sign (<code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">S</code>) characters define purely <i><dfn>numeric</dfn></i> data items, while picture specifications containing alphabetic (<code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">A</code>) or alphanumeric (<code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">X</code>) characters define <i><dfn>alphanumeric</dfn></i> data items. The presence of other formatting characters define <i><dfn>edited numeric</dfn></i> or <i><dfn>edited alphanumeric</dfn></i> data items.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7_13.18.40_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7_13.18.40-124">[121]</a></sup></p>/n<table class="wikitable">/n<caption>Examples</caption>/n<tr>/n<th><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">PICTURE</code> clause</th>/n<th>Value in</th>/n<th>Value out</th>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td rowspan="2"><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="kt">PIC 9(5)</span></code></td>/n<td><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">100</code></td>/n<td><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">00100</code></td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">"Hello"</code></td>/n<td><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">"Hello"</code> (this is legal, but results in <a href="/wiki/Undefined_behavior" title="Undefined behavior">undefined behavior</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7_14.9.24_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7_14.9.24-122">[119]</a></sup></td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="kt">PIC +++++</span></code></td>/n<td><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">-10</code></td>/n<td><code>"&#160;&#160;-10"</code> (note leading spaces)</td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="kt">PIC 99/99/9(4)</span></code></td>/n<td><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">31042003</code></td>/n<td><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">"31/04/2003"</code></td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td rowspan="2"><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="kt">PIC *(4)9.99</span></code></td>/n<td><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">100.50</code></td>/n<td><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">"**100.50"</code></td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td><code>0</code></td>/n<td><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">"****0.00"</code></td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="kt">PIC X(3)BX(3)BX(3)</span></code></td>/n<td><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">"ABCDEFGHI"</code></td>/n<td><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">"ABC DEF GHI"</code></td>/n</tr>/n</table>/n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="USAGE_clause">USAGE clause</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=COBOL&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: USAGE clause">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>/n<p>The <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">USAGE</code> clause declares the format data is stored in. Depending on the data type, it can either complement or be used instead of a <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">PICTURE</code> clause. While it can be used to declare pointers and object references, it is mostly geared towards specifying numeric types. These numeric formats are:<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7_13.18.60.3_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7_13.18.60.3-125">[122]</a></sup></p>/n<ul>/n<li>Binary, where a minimum size is either specified by the <code>PICTURE</code> clause or by a <code>USAGE</code> clause such as <code>BINARY-LONG</code>.</li>/n<li><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="kp">USAGE</span> <span class="kt">COMPUTATIONAL</span></code>, where data may be stored in whatever format the implementation provides; often equivalent to &#160;<code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="kp">USAGE</span> <span class="kt">BINARY</span></code></li>/n<li><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="kp">USAGE</span> <span class="kr">DISPLAY</span></code>, the default format, where data is stored as a string</li>/n<li>Floating-point, in either an implementation-dependent format or according to IEEE 754.</li>/n<li><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="kp">USAGE</span> <span class="kp">NATIONAL</span></code>, where data is stored as a string using an extended character set</li>/n<li><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="kp">USAGE</span> <span class="kp">PACKED-DECIMAL</span></code>, where data is stored in the smallest possible decimal format (typically <a href="/wiki/Packed_binary-coded_decimal" class="mw-redirect" title="Packed binary-coded decimal">packed binary-coded decimal</a>)</li>/n</ul>/n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Report_writer">Report writer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=COBOL&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Report writer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>/n<p>The report writer is a <a href="/wiki/Declarative_programming" title="Declarative programming">declarative</a> facility for creating reports. The programmer need only specify the report layout and the data required to produce it, freeing them from having to write code to handle things like page breaks, data formatting, and headings and footings.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014855_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014855-126">[123]</a></sup></p>/n<p>Reports are associated with report files, which are files which may only be written to through report writer statements.</p>/n<div class="mw-highlight mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">/n<pre>/n<span class="c">      </span> <span class="kr">FD </span> <span class="nv">report-out</span> <span class="kp">REPORT</span> <span class="nv">sales-report</span><span class="p">.</span>/n</pre></div>/n<p>Each report is defined in the report section of the data division. A report is split into report groups which define the report's headings, footings and details. Reports work around hierarchical <i><dfn>control breaks</dfn></i>. Control breaks occur when a key variable changes it value; for example, when creating a report detailing customers' orders, a control break could occur when the program reaches a different customer's orders. Here is an example report description for a report which gives a salesperson's sales and which warns of any invalid records:</p>/n<div class="mw-highlight mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">/n<pre>/n<span class="c">      </span> <span class="kp">RD </span> <span class="nv">sales-report</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="kp">PAGE</span> <span class="kp">LIMITS</span> <span class="mi">60 </span><span class="kp">LINES</span>/n<span class="kp">          </span> <span class="kp">FIRST</span> <span class="kp">DETAIL</span> <span class="mi">3</span>/n<span class="mi">           </span><span class="kp">CONTROLS</span> <span class="nv">seller-name</span><span class="p">.</span>/n/n<span class="c">      </span> <span class="mi">01  </span><span class="kp">TYPE</span> <span class="kp">PAGE</span> <span class="kp">HEADING</span><span class="p">.</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="mi">03  </span><span class="kp">COL</span> <span class="mi">1                    </span><span class="kp">VALUE </span><span class="s2">"Sales Report"</span><span class="p">.</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="mi">03  </span><span class="kp">COL</span> <span class="mi">74                   </span><span class="kp">VALUE </span><span class="s2">"Page"</span><span class="p">.</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="mi">03  </span><span class="kp">COL</span> <span class="mi">79                   </span><span class="kt">PIC Z9</span> <span class="kp">SOURCE</span> <span class="err">PAGE-COUNTER</span><span class="p">.</span>/n/n<span class="c">      </span> <span class="mi">01  </span><span class="nv">sales-on-day</span> <span class="kp">TYPE</span> <span class="kp">DETAIL</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="kp">LINE </span><span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">.</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="mi">03  </span><span class="kp">COL</span> <span class="mi">3                    </span><span class="kp">VALUE </span><span class="s2">"Sales on"</span><span class="p">.</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="mi">03  </span><span class="kp">COL</span> <span class="mi">12                   </span><span class="kt">PIC 99/99/9999</span> <span class="kp">SOURCE</span> <span class="nv">sales-date</span><span class="p">.</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="mi">03  </span><span class="kp">COL</span> <span class="mi">21                   </span><span class="kp">VALUE </span><span class="s2">"were"</span><span class="p">.</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="mi">03  </span><span class="kp">COL</span> <span class="mi">26                   </span><span class="kt">PIC $$$$9.99</span> <span class="kp">SOURCE</span> <span class="nv">sales-amount</span><span class="p">.</span>/n/n<span class="c">      </span> <span class="mi">01  </span><span class="nv">invalid-sales</span> <span class="kp">TYPE</span> <span class="kp">DETAIL</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="kp">LINE </span><span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">.</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="mi">03  </span><span class="kp">COL</span> <span class="mi">3                    </span><span class="kp">VALUE </span><span class="s2">"INVALID RECORD:"</span><span class="p">.</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="mi">03  </span><span class="kp">COL</span> <span class="mi">19                   </span><span class="kt">PIC X(34)</span> <span class="kp">SOURCE</span> <span class="nv">sales-record</span><span class="p">.</span>/n/n<span class="c">      </span> <span class="mi">01  </span><span class="kp">TYPE</span> <span class="kp">CONTROL</span> <span class="kp">HEADING</span> <span class="nv">seller-name</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="kp">LINE </span><span class="o">+</span> <span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">.</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="mi">03  </span><span class="kp">COL</span> <span class="mi">1                    </span><span class="kp">VALUE </span><span class="s2">"Seller:"</span><span class="p">.</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="mi">03  </span><span class="kp">COL</span> <span class="mi">9                    </span><span class="kt">PIC X(30)</span> <span class="kp">SOURCE</span> <span class="nv">seller-name</span><span class="p">.</span>/n</pre></div>/n<p>The above report description describes the following layout:</p>/n<pre>/nSales Report                                                             Page  1/n/nSeller: Howard Bromberg/n  Sales on 10/12/2008 were $1000.00/n  Sales on 12/12/2008 were    $0.00/n  Sales on 13/12/2008 were   $31.47/n  INVALID RECORD: Howard Bromberg             XXXXYY/n/nSeller: Howard Discount/n.../nSales Report                                                            Page 12/n/n  Sales on 08/05/2014 were  $543.98/n  INVALID RECORD: William Selden      12O52014FOOFOO/n  Sales on 30/05/2014 were    $0.00/n</pre>/n<p>Four statements control the report writer: <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">INITIATE</code>, which prepares the report writer for printing; <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">GENERATE</code>, which prints a report group; <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">SUPPRESS</code>, which suppresses the printing of a report group; and <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">TERMINATE</code>, which terminates report processing. For the above sales report example, the procedure division might look like this:</p>/n<div class="mw-highlight mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">/n<pre>/n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="kr">OPEN</span> <span class="kp">INPUT</span> <span class="nv">sales</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="kp">OUTPUT</span> <span class="nv">report-out</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="kr">INITIATE</span> <span class="nv">sales-report</span>/n /n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="kr">PERFORM</span> <span class="kp">UNTIL</span> <span class="mi">1 </span><span class="o">&lt;&gt;</span> <span class="mi">1</span>/n<span class="mi">               </span><span class="kr">READ</span> <span class="nv">sales</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>             <span class="kp">AT</span> <span class="kr">END</span>/n<span class="kr">                      </span> <span class="kr">EXIT</span> <span class="kr">PERFORM</span>/n<span class="kr">              </span> <span class="kr">END-READ</span>/n<span class="kr"> </span>/n<span class="kr">              </span> <span class="kr">VALIDATE</span> <span class="nv">sales-record</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>         <span class="kr">IF</span> <span class="nv">valid-record</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>             <span class="kr">GENERATE</span> <span class="nv">sales-on-day</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>         <span class="kr">ELSE</span>/n<span class="kr">                  </span> <span class="kr">GENERATE</span> <span class="nv">invalid-sales</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>         <span class="kr">END-IF</span>/n<span class="kr">          </span> <span class="kr">END-PERFORM</span>/n<span class="kr"> </span>/n<span class="kr">          </span> <span class="kr">TERMINATE</span> <span class="nv">sales-report</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="kr">CLOSE</span> <span class="nv">sales</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="nv">report-out</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="p">.</span>/n</pre></div>/n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Procedure_division">Procedure division</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=COBOL&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Procedure division">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Procedures">Procedures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=COBOL&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Procedures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>/n<p>The sections and paragraphs in the procedure division (collectively called procedures) can be used as <a href="/wiki/Label_(programming)" class="mw-redirect" title="Label (programming)">labels</a> and as simple <a href="/wiki/Subroutines" class="mw-redirect" title="Subroutines">subroutines</a>. Unlike in other divisions, paragraphs do not need to be in sections.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7_14.4_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7_14.4-127">[124]</a></sup> Execution goes down through the procedures of a program until it is terminated.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7_14.6.3_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7_14.6.3-128">[125]</a></sup> To use procedures as subroutines, the <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">PERFORM</code> verb is used. This transfers control to the specified range of procedures and returns only upon reaching the end.</p>/n<div class="thumb tleft">/n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:COBOL_Mine.svg" class="image"><img alt="PROCEDURE DIVISION. PERFORM update-screen. GOBACK. fix-screen SECTION. MOVE &quot;Error fixed&quot; TO screen-line. PERFORM update-screen. update-screen SECTION. IF invalid-screen, GO TO fix-screen. END-IF." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/COBOL_Mine.svg/170px-COBOL_Mine.svg.png" width="170" height="240" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/COBOL_Mine.svg/255px-COBOL_Mine.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/COBOL_Mine.svg/340px-COBOL_Mine.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="744" data-file-height="1052" /></a>/n<div class="thumbcaption">/n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:COBOL_Mine.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>/nA mine is "armed" when the screen is invalid.</div>/n</div>/n</div>/n<p>Unusual control flow can trigger <i><dfn>mines</dfn></i>, which cause control in performed procedures to return at unexpected times to unexpected locations. Procedures can be reached in three ways: they can be called with <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">PERFORM</code>, jumped to from a <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">GO TO</code> or through execution "falling through" the bottom of an above paragraph. Combinations of these invoke <a href="/wiki/Undefined_behavior" title="Undefined behavior">undefined behavior</a>, creating mines. Specifically, mines occur when execution of a range of procedures would cause control flow to go past the last statement of a range of procedures already being performed.<sup id="cite_ref-FR99_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FR99-129">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-VV07_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VV07-130">[127]</a></sup></p>/n<p>For example, in the code in the adjacent image, a mine is tripped at the end of <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">update-screen</code> when the screen is invalid. When the screen is invalid, control jumps to the <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">fix-screen</code> section, which, when done, performs <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">update-screen</code>. This recursion triggers undefined behavior as there are now two overlapping ranges of procedures being performed. The mine is then triggered upon reaching the end of <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">update-screen</code> and means control could return to one of two locations:</p>/n<ul>/n<li>The first <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">PERFORM</code> statement</li>/n<li>The <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">PERFORM</code> statement in <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">fix-screen</code>, where it would then "fall-through" into <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">update-screen</code> and return to the first <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">PERFORM</code> statement upon reaching the end.</li>/n</ul>/n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Statements">Statements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=COBOL&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Statements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>/n<p>COBOL 2014 has 47 statements (also called <i><dfn>verbs</dfn></i>),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG42014.C2.A7_14.9_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG42014.C2.A7_14.9-131">[128]</a></sup> which can be grouped into the following broad categories: control flow, I/O, data manipulation and the report writer. The report writer statements are covered in the <a href="#Report_writer">report writer section</a>.</p>/n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Control_flow">Control flow</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=COBOL&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Control flow">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>/n<p>COBOL's <a href="/wiki/Conditional_(computer_programming)" title="Conditional (computer programming)">conditional statements</a> are <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">IF</code> and <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">EVALUATE</code>. <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">EVALUATE</code> is a <a href="/wiki/Switch_statement" title="Switch statement">switch-like statement</a> with the added capability of evaluating multiple values and conditions. This can be used to implement <a href="/wiki/Decision_table" title="Decision table">decision tables</a>. For example, the following might be used to control a <a href="/wiki/CNC_lathe" class="mw-redirect" title="CNC lathe">CNC lathe</a>:</p>/n<div class="mw-highlight mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">/n<pre>/n<span class="kr">EVALUATE</span> <span class="nb">TRUE</span> <span class="kp">ALSO</span> <span class="nv">desired-speed</span> <span class="kp">ALSO</span> <span class="nv">current-speed</span>/n    <span class="kp">WHEN</span> <span class="nv">lid-closed</span> <span class="kp">ALSO</span> <span class="nv">min-speed</span> <span class="kp">THRU</span> <span class="nv">max-speed</span> <span class="kp">ALSO</span> <span class="ow">LESS</span> <span class="ow">THAN</span> <span class="nv">desired-speed</span>/n        <span class="kr">PERFORM</span> <span class="nv">speed-up-machine</span>/n    <span class="kp">WHEN</span> <span class="nv">lid-closed</span> <span class="kp">ALSO</span> <span class="nv">min-speed</span> <span class="kp">THRU</span> <span class="nv">max-speed</span> <span class="kp">ALSO</span> <span class="ow">GREATER</span> <span class="ow">THAN</span> <span class="nv">desired-speed</span>/n        <span class="kr">PERFORM</span> <span class="nv">slow-down-machine</span>/n    <span class="kp">WHEN</span> <span class="nv">lid-open</span> <span class="kp">ALSO</span> <span class="nv">ANY</span> <span class="kp">ALSO</span> <span class="ow">NOT</span> <span class="no">ZERO</span>/n<span class="no">       </span> <span class="kr">PERFORM</span> <span class="nv">emergency-stop</span>/n    <span class="kp">WHEN</span> <span class="kp">OTHER</span>/n<span class="kp">       </span> <span class="kr">CONTINUE</span>/n<span class="kr">END-EVALUATE</span>/n</pre></div>/n<p>The <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">PERFORM</code> statement is used to define loops which are executed <em>until</em> a condition is true (not <em>while</em> true, which is more common in other languages). It is also used to call procedures or ranges of procedures (see the <a href="#Procedures">procedures section</a> for more details). <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">CALL</code> and <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">INVOKE</code> call subprograms and methods, respectively. The name of the subprogram/method is contained in a string which may be a literal or a data item.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7.C2.A7_14.9.4.2C_14.9.22_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7.C2.A7_14.9.4.2C_14.9.22-132">[129]</a></sup> Parameters can be passed <a href="/wiki/Call_by_reference" class="mw-redirect" title="Call by reference">by reference</a>, by content (where a copy is passed by reference) or <a href="/wiki/Call_by_value" class="mw-redirect" title="Call by value">by value</a> (but only if a <a href="/wiki/Function_prototype" title="Function prototype">prototype</a> is available).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7_D.6.5.2.2_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7_D.6.5.2.2-133">[130]</a></sup> <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">CANCEL</code> unloads subprograms from memory. <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">GO TO</code> causes the program to jump to a specified procedure.</p>/n<p>The <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">GOBACK</code> statement is a <a href="/wiki/Return_statement" title="Return statement">return statement</a> and the <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">STOP</code> statement stops the program. The <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">EXIT</code> statement has six different formats: it can be used as a return statement, a <a href="/wiki/Break_statement" class="mw-redirect" title="Break statement">break statement</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Continue_statement" class="mw-redirect" title="Continue statement">continue statement</a>, an end marker or to leave a procedure.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7_14.9.13.1_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A7_14.9.13.1-134">[131]</a></sup></p>/n<p><a href="/wiki/Exception_handling" title="Exception handling">Exceptions</a> are raised by a <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">RAISE</code> statement and caught with a handler, or <i><dfn>declarative</dfn></i>, defined in the <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">DECLARATIVES</code> portion of the procedure division. Declaratives are sections beginning with a <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">USE</code> statement which specify the errors to handle. Exceptions can be names or objects. <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">RESUME</code> is used in a declarative to jump to the statement after the one that raised the exception or to a procedure outside the <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">DECLARATIVES</code>. Unlike other languages, uncaught exceptions may not terminate the program and the program can proceed unaffected.</p>/n<h5><span id="I/O"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="I.2FO">I/O</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=COBOL&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: I/O">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>/n<p>File I/O is handled by the self-describing <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">OPEN</code>, <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">CLOSE</code>, <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">READ</code>, and <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">WRITE</code> statements along with a further three: <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">REWRITE</code>, which updates a record; <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">START</code>, which selects subsequent records to access by finding a record with a certain key; and <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">UNLOCK</code>, which releases a <a href="/wiki/Lock_(database)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lock (database)">lock</a> on the last record accessed.</p>/n<p>User interaction is done using <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">ACCEPT</code> and <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">DISPLAY</code>.</p>/n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Data_manipulation">Data manipulation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=COBOL&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Data manipulation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>/n<p>The following verbs manipulate data:</p>/n<ul>/n<li><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">INITIALIZE</code>, which sets data items to their default values.</li>/n<li><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">MOVE</code>, which <a href="/wiki/Assignment_(computer_science)" title="Assignment (computer science)">assigns</a> values to data items.</li>/n<li><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">SET</code>, which has 15 formats: it can modify indices, assign object references and alter table capacities, among other functions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A714.9.35.1_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014.C2.A714.9.35.1-135">[132]</a></sup></li>/n<li><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">ADD</code>, <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">SUBTRACT</code>, <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">MULTIPLY</code>, <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">DIVIDE</code>, and <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">COMPUTE</code>, which handle arithmetic (with <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">COMPUTE</code> assigning the result of a formula to a variable).</li>/n<li><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">ALLOCATE</code> and <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">FREE</code>, which handle <a href="/wiki/Dynamic_memory" class="mw-redirect" title="Dynamic memory">dynamic memory</a>.</li>/n<li><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">VALIDATE</code>, which validates and distributes data as specified in an item's description in the data division.</li>/n<li><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">STRING</code> and <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">UNSTRING</code>, which <a href="/wiki/Concatenation" title="Concatenation">concatenate</a> and split <a href="/wiki/String_(computer_science)" title="String (computer science)">strings</a>, respectively.</li>/n<li><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">INSPECT</code>, which tallies or replaces instances of specified <a href="/wiki/Substring" title="Substring">substrings</a> within a string.</li>/n<li><code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">SEARCH</code>, which searches a table for the first entry satisfying a condition.</li>/n</ul>/n<p>Files and tables are sorted using <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">SORT</code> and the <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">MERGE</code> verb merges and sorts files. The <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">RELEASE</code> verb provides records to sort and <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">RETURN</code> retrieves sorted records in order.</p>/n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Scope_termination">Scope termination</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=COBOL&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Scope termination">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>/n<p>Some statements, such as <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">IF</code> and <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">READ</code>, may themselves contain statements. Such statements may be terminated in two ways: by a period (<i><dfn>implicit termination</dfn></i>), which terminates <i>all</i> unterminated statements contained, or by a scope terminator, which terminates the nearest matching open statement.</p>/n<div class="mw-highlight mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">/n<pre>/n<span class="c">*&gt; Terminator period ("implicit termination")</span>/n<span class="kr">IF</span> <span class="nv">invalid-record</span>/n    <span class="kr">IF</span> <span class="nv">no-more-records</span>/n        <span class="kp">NEXT</span> <span class="kp">SENTENCE</span>/n<span class="kp">   </span> <span class="kr">ELSE</span>/n<span class="kr">       </span> <span class="kr">READ</span> <span class="nv">record-file</span>/n            <span class="kp">AT</span> <span class="kr">END</span> <span class="kr">SET</span> <span class="nv">no-more-records</span> <span class="kp">TO</span> <span class="nb">TRUE</span><span class="p">.</span>/n/n<span class="c">*&gt; Scope terminators ("explicit termination")</span>/n<span class="kr">IF</span> <span class="nv">invalid-record</span>/n    <span class="kr">IF</span> <span class="nv">no-more-records</span>/n        <span class="kr">CONTINUE</span>/n<span class="kr">   </span> <span class="kr">ELSE</span>/n<span class="kr">       </span> <span class="kr">READ</span> <span class="nv">record-file</span>/n            <span class="kp">AT</span> <span class="kr">END</span> <span class="kr">SET</span> <span class="nv">no-more-records</span> <span class="kp">TO</span> <span class="nb">TRUE</span>/n<span class="nb">       </span> <span class="kr">END-READ</span>/n<span class="kr">   </span> <span class="kr">END-IF</span>/n<span class="kr">END-IF</span>/n</pre></div>/n<p>Nested statements terminated with a period are a common source of bugs.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014899_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42014899-136">[133]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcCrackenGolden1988.C2.A7_8.4_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcCrackenGolden1988.C2.A7_8.4-137">[134]</a></sup> For example, examine the following code:</p>/n<div class="mw-highlight mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">/n<pre>/n<span class="kr">IF</span> <span class="nv">x</span>/n    <span class="kr">DISPLAY</span> <span class="nv">y</span><span class="p">.</span>/n    <span class="kr">DISPLAY</span> <span class="nv">z</span><span class="p">.</span>/n</pre></div>/n<p>Here, the intent is to display <code>y</code> and <code>z</code> if condition <code>x</code> is true. However, <code>z</code> will be displayed whatever the value of <code>x</code> because the <code>IF</code> statement is terminated by an erroneous period after <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="kr">DISPLAY</span> <span class="nv">y</span></code>.</p>/n<p>Another bug is a result of the <a href="/wiki/Dangling_else_problem" class="mw-redirect" title="Dangling else problem">dangling else problem</a>, when two <code>IF</code> statements can associate with an <code>ELSE</code>.</p>/n<div class="mw-highlight mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">/n<pre>/n<span class="kr">IF</span> <span class="nv">x</span>/n    <span class="kr">IF</span> <span class="nv">y</span>/n        <span class="kr">DISPLAY</span> <span class="nv">a</span>/n<span class="kr">ELSE</span>/n<span class="kr">   </span> <span class="kr">DISPLAY</span> <span class="nv">b</span><span class="p">.</span>/n</pre></div>/n<p>In the above fragment, the <code>ELSE</code> associates with the &#160;<code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="kr">IF</span> <span class="nv">y</span></code>&#160; statement instead of the &#160;<code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="kr">IF</span> <span class="nv">x</span></code>&#160; statement, causing a bug. Prior to the introduction of explicit scope terminators, preventing it would require &#160;<code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="kr">ELSE</span> <span class="kp">NEXT</span> <span class="kp">SENTENCE</span></code>&#160; to be placed after the inner <code>IF</code>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcCrackenGolden1988.C2.A7_8.4_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcCrackenGolden1988.C2.A7_8.4-137">[134]</a></sup></p>/n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Self-modifying_code">Self-modifying code</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=COBOL&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Self-modifying code">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>/n<p>The original (1959) COBOL specification supported the infamous &#160;<code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="kp">ALTER</span> <span class="nv">X</span> <span class="kp">TO</span> <span class="kp">PROCEED</span> <span class="kp">TO</span> <span class="nv">Y</span></code>&#160; statement, for which many compilers generated <a href="/wiki/Self-modifying_code" title="Self-modifying code">self-modifying code</a>. <code>X</code> and <code>Y</code> are procedure labels, and the single &#160;<code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="kr">GO</span> <span class="kp">TO</span></code>&#160; statement in procedure <code>X</code> executed after such an <code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr">ALTER</code> statement means &#160;<code class="mw-highlight" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="kr">GO</span> <span class="kp">TO</span> <span class="nv">Y</span></code>&#160; instead. Many compilers still support it,<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[135]</a></sup> but it was deemed <a href="/wiki/Deprecation" title="Deprecation">obsolete</a> in the COBOL 1985 standard and deleted in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42001.C2.A7_F.1_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEISO.2FIEC_JTC_1.2FSC_22.2FWG_42001.C2.A7_F.1-139">[136]</a></sup></p>/n<h3><span id="Hello,_world"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Hello.2C_world">Hello, world</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=COBOL&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Hello, world">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>/n<p>A "<a href="/wiki/Hello,_world" class="mw-redirect" title="Hello, world">Hello, world</a>" program in COBOL:</p>/n<div class="mw-highlight mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">/n<pre>/n<span class="c">      </span> <span class="kr">IDENTIFICATION</span> <span class="kr">DIVISION</span><span class="p">.</span>/n<span class="c">      </span> <span class="kr">PROGRAM-ID</span><span class="p">.</span> <span class="nv">hello-world</span><span class="p">.</span>/n<span class="c">      </span> <span class="kr">PROCEDURE</span> <span class="kr">DIVISION</span><span class="p">.</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="kr">DISPLAY </span><span class="s2">"Hello, world!"</span>/n<span class="c">      </span>     <span class="p">.</span>/n</pre></div>/n<p>When the – now famous – <a href="/wiki/%22Hello,_World!%22_program" title="&quot;Hello, World!&quot; program">"Hello, World!" program</a> example in <i><a href="/wiki/The_C_Programming_Language_(book)" class="mw-redirect" title="The C Programming Language (book)">The C Programming Language</a></i> was first published in 1978 a similar mainframe COBOL program sample would have been submitted through <a href="/wiki/Job_Control_Language" title="Job Control Language">JCL</a>, very likely using a punch card reader, and 80 column punch cards. The listing below, <i>with an empty DATA DIVISION</i>, was tested using GNU/Linux and the System/370 <a href="/wiki/Hercules_emulator" class="mw-redirect" title="Hercules emulator">Hercules emulator</a> running <a href="/wiki/MVS" title="MVS">MVS</a> 3.8J. The JCL, written in July 2015, is derived from the Hercules tutorials and samples hosted by Jay Moseley.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[137]</a></sup> In keeping with COBOL programming of that era, HELLO, WORLD is displayed in all capital letters.</p>/n<div class="mw-highlight mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">/n<pre>/n<span class="o">//</span><span class="nv">COBUCLG</span>  <span class="nv">JOB</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">001</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="s1">'COBOL BASE TEST'</span><span class="p">,</span> class="p">,</span><span class="nv">DISP</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="nv">SHR</span>                           <span class="mi">00200000</span>/n<span class="o">//</span><span class="kr">GO</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="nv">SYSPRINT</span> <span class="nv">DD</span> <span class="nv">SYSOUT</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="nv">A</span>                                               <span class="mi">00210000</span>/n<span class="o">//</span>                                                                      <span class="mi">00220000</span>/n</pre></div>/n<p>After submitting the JCL, the MVS console displayed:</p>/n<div class="mw-highlight mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">/n<pre>/n    19.52.48 JOB    3  $HASP100 COBUCLG  ON READER1     COBOL BASE TEST/n    19.52.48 JOB    3  IEF677I WARNING MESSAGE(S) FOR JOB COBUCLG  ISSUED/n    19.52.48 JOB    3  $HASP373 COBUCLG  STARTED - INIT  1 - CLASS A - SYS BSP1/n
